Record of the General Meeting of the Red Cross Society

Resolved to Invite Chairman Wang Yiting to Preside over the Meeting

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the Chinese Red Cross Society held a temporary meeting of member representatives at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association on the second floor. Sixty to seventy people attended. Hu Hongji, a representative from the National Government, and Yan Sen, a representative from the Municipal Government, attended. Wang Peiyuan, Zhou Guangjiu, and Wang Fuqing were publicly elected as chairmen, and Ji Zhongze and Ji Heqin were appointed as recorders. After performing the rituals, the chairman reported on how the first vote had not been completed, leading to a re-election, which was also illegal. They discussed how this should be resolved and that the qualifications of the attending representatives should be strictly reviewed before the meeting to avoid repeating the same mistakes. Jiang Daqiu proposed the election of three people as a review committee. The chairman submitted it for a vote, and there were no objections. Member Dong Xinqin proposed that there was no quorum of representatives. The chairman replied that according to Article 54 of the charter, the resolutions of the general meeting of members were limited to the number of attending members. Dong said that the principles of civil rights must be followed. Member Ji Heqin said that the highest organ of the association was the Standing Council. Since the revolutionary army secured the Yangtze River, not a single motion had complied with the principles of civil rights, and no one had mentioned basing things on the principles of civil rights. The chairman invited Municipal Government representative Yan Sen to speak. Yan said that the government had not yet decided on the election for your association and that to respect your association, all unresolved issues should be resolved by your association itself. The government would not intervene, but it was not easy to convene a meeting, and the government had sent someone to investigate after the dispute arose. They knew that there was a proposal to convene a temporary meeting on August 10. The government hoped for success because procedural issues had to be carefully considered. After the meeting, each member would raise their spirits, take responsibility, and develop the future. The government would not interfere. Under these circumstances, it was hoped that the association would quickly reorganize itself. Today's chairman had not arrived, which was not in accordance with the charter, but the government's meaning had been stated in the newspaper. The four items that were to be handled today were issues of the association itself, not government issues. The government's responsibility was supervision and it could not resolve legislative issues for your association. The situation today should be reported to the government for reference and decision. The government could not advise on whether the meeting could be held or whether it was legal because there was a charter to follow. Representative Jiang Daqiu of the Huai'an branch proposed to publicly invite the chairman to attend the meeting, and more than five people seconded the motion. Dong Xinqin proposed to retroactively recognize today's meeting as a discussion meeting, which was approved by all. As a result, Ji Heqin was publicly elected to draft a telegram to Wang Yiting: "Representatives have arrived at the meeting and generally agree that the meeting cannot be held without the chairman's attendance. We urgently hope that you will come to Shanghai immediately. The public is deeply expectant. The representatives and members attending the Third Temporary General Meeting of the Chinese Red Cross Society kowtow." Member Ji Heqin proposed that if the chairman had asked for leave three days ago, Mr. Huang Han should act on his behalf. Mr. Huang took responsibility and held two Standing Council meetings and one Executive Committee meeting within five days. Today, he suddenly sent a letter saying that he was suffering from diarrhea and hemorrhoids. Why would he be robust for Li Yingguang's scheme to become chairman but succumb to illness today? There were only three Standing Council members who attended the meeting. Mr. Yao Yuqin sat down briefly and left. Mr. Yuan Zhongwei and Ha Shaofu were still present. Why were the councilors who could attend a meeting two days ago unable to come today? If the chairman and councilors use passive methods to resist and make it impossible for the meeting to be held, we will only have to request the government to send someone to supervise and have the branch associations publicly elect representatives to take over the headquarters. Everyone applauded and supported this proposal. Dong Xinqin proposed that if the chairman pretends to be ill and does not come, we will send representatives to respectfully request his presence. Li Zhenbang of the Taian branch proposed that now that there are natural disasters and man-made disasters everywhere, and corpses are lying unburied, rescue and protection are the responsibility of our Red Cross Society. Why are the gentlemen of the Standing Council standing idly by? The Red Cross constitution stipulates that a meeting is held every three years. Why has it not been held for eight years? Although it was held this year, the dates were changed, changed, and changed again, a total of four or five times. Now there is a letter and telegram notification to hold a meeting on August 10, and the branches are sending representatives to Shanghai. The Standing Council sent a letter inviting them to go to the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association at 2:00 PM this afternoon. Why did the chairman, vice-chairman, etc. of the Standing Council not attend? In such hot weather, our branch representatives and members are suffering in vain, and the association's affairs are unnamed and trifling. I very much support the items proposed by the gentlemen. If the chairman does not come, we will prepare our own travel expenses to go to Ningbo to hold a meeting. Everyone applauded and supported the proposal and then dispersed.

Workers at the Lianglu General Factory Re-Raise Demands

Director Liu Scheduled to Reply on Monday

The artisans of the Wusong General Factory of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Ningbo Railways, due to the recent impact of gold prices on their livelihood and the difficulty of maintaining a living, requested rice subsidies and housing allowances from the Railway Bureau the other day, as reported in the Japanese newspaper on the 9th. It is now known that the artisans waited quietly for a resolution because the person in charge of the factory promised to relay everything to Director Liu for explanation. However, as there was still no response as of yesterday, the labor union re-submitted this request and asked the railway authorities to explain why those with salaries above 100 yuan received a 25% housing allowance, while those with salaries below 100 yuan received nothing. At this time of high prices, it inevitably made those who enjoyed huge salaries feel richer economically, while low-paid employees who were in dire straits were increasingly unable to make ends meet, and the authorities had not issued any remedial measures. This was unfair in both reason and emotion. It was also stipulated that the rice subsidy must be based on a rice price of 12 yuan as the highest, and if the market price rose to 20 yuan, each person must be given a rice subsidy of 8 yuan per month, which would be issued at the end of each month along with the monthly salary. As for housing allowances, all those below 100 yuan would receive an additional 25% of their salary to show fair treatment, and the Railway Bureau was given 20 hours to reply. Liu Weichi, the Director of the Railway Bureau, summoned Cai Jinhai and other representatives of the factory yesterday afternoon to explain everything. The representatives also stated their opinions and requested that the railway authorities accommodate them. Director Liu accepted the request and promised to relay it to Minister Sun this Thursday and give an official reply next Monday, hoping that all workers would wait quietly for a resolution.

Xiang Sheng Factory Resolves Rice Subsidy Issue

The issue of workers at the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory in Lujiazui, Pudong, requesting an increase in rice subsidies of 2 yuan per person per month from the employer was reported in the previous newspaper. It is now known that the request was successfully resolved yesterday. The employer agreed to increase each worker's wages by 5 cents of silver each day, which was only half a yuan less than the original request per month, and claimed that it was because the factory's business was slack. This was not a lack of consideration. Labor representatives Zhang Linhua, a standing committee member of the labor union, and translator Xia Zhenru negotiated back and forth, and both sides agreed to this request, which was approved to be implemented on August 13. It was also heard that the labor union's affiliated voluntary elementary school was overcrowded with new students this semester, and the existing classrooms were insufficient, so they rented a room from the Japanese-Chinese Workers' Union building as a classroom. At the same time, they requested an increase in subsidies from the factory, which was also approved by the factory foremen, Peng Si and Tang Baluo, to increase the subsidy by 40 yuan per month.

Yesterday's News on the Strike of the French Concession Water and Electricity Workers

The French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Union had originally scheduled to convene a general meeting at the Public Sports Ground yesterday afternoon, but it was changed to a discussion meeting at the union's office on Luban Road at 4:00 PM for other reasons. More than 700 members attended. Xu A'mei was publicly elected as chairman. After performing the rituals, the chairman reported that the union had sent representatives Lu Guanhong, Shen Keming, Xu A'mei, and Zhang Renjun to inquire with the Municipal Party Department about the Central Party Department's mediation of the case. Comrade Chen Junyi, a standing committee member of the Municipal People's Training Association, received them and said that Mr. Li Shizeng of the Central Government was actively mediating the matter and had negotiated with the French Consul several times regarding the preconditions proposed by the union. A satisfactory resolution should be reached soon, and the union was asked to wait patiently for the mediation of the higher authorities. The preconditions were as follows: (1) The French authorities were requested to release the arrested workers as soon as possible. (2) The issue of wage increases was that each person would receive an additional 2 yuan and 4 jiao of silver per month. (3) The factory would pay the wages of the workers during the strike period. (4) The issue of the employer dismissing workers would be mediated by Mr. Li Shizeng, and all dismissed workers would be allowed to work in the union office, with their monthly wages paid by the factory. This matter was still under negotiation, and if there were results, representatives from both labor and management would be convened to discuss it and resolve it. Finally, the following resolutions were discussed: (1) What should be done about the case of union worker Zhou Longhu being captured by Wang Wenjie, Wu Qinsheng, and Yuan Along when he passed by the company's gate, severely beaten, and sent to the police station? It was resolved to submit a request to higher authorities for a prompt and serious negotiation. (2) A request should be submitted to the Municipal Party Department for the protection of human rights in the case of worker spies privately capturing loyal workers.

Telegram from Two Postal Unions to Minister Wang

Telegram from the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, etc., to Minister Wang of the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing: We are greatly relieved that the Shanghai postal workers, in order to resolve the ten outstanding cases, were about to cause a major storm. Fortunately, you have shown consideration for the situation and have insight into the crux of the postal workers' suffering, and have specially sent a commissioner to consult with our union, etc. Director-General Wei has also met with us with sincerity, and we have been able to bring this to a close in this time of crisis and achieve a satisfactory resolution. Our union, on behalf of the postal workers nationwide, would like to express our sincere thanks to you. However, there is something we must say: all of our postal workers are inspired by the righteousness of our party, and we are more sincere in our love and protection of the post office than anyone else. As for the ten outstanding cases, they are all about the improvement of postal construction, the preservation of the post office's original good system, and the improvement of the lives of postal workers across the country. Our postal workers have studied these cases and unanimously believe that if the previous postal authorities could have studied them with the slightest sincerity, it would not have been difficult to accept them on the day they were proposed. Why did they delay them for a year, resulting in these outstanding cases? The previous postal authorities' disregard for the demands of our union, etc., was the main reason for causing this storm. During this year, our union, etc., endured pain and bitterness, eagerly anticipating a result like this, which is why we had to give a limited-time response. Our union, etc., deeply knows the difficulty of building the post office and does not want to cause a storm to create various unfortunate disputes. Therefore, in this serious situation, we remained calm and sought a final solution. Fortunately, with your wise observation and the assistance of Director-General Wei, the cases were satisfactorily resolved under the consultation of both parties on August 4, which is gratifying. From this, we know that none of the demands put forward by our union, etc., are unreasonable or unsolvable, but can be resolved by opening up and consulting in good faith. We hope that in the future, you will abandon your suspicions and eliminate the barriers to our union's suggestions and meet us with sincerity. If our postal workers are not mindless or insane, they will never harm the post office, which is the foundation of their survival. If you adopt this suggestion, the future of the post office will depend on it. We respectfully await your enlightened teachings. Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, Shanghai Postal Employees' Union, together with our respect.

Shanghai Federation Issues Declaration

Regarding Foreign Insurance Companies

According to the Guo Wen News Agency, the Shanghai Federation of Citizens issued a declaration yesterday regarding foreign insurance companies: The Fuzhou Guild recently informed various groups that on November 5, 1928, the Xin Ji steamship of the China Merchants Bureau was loaded with goods and set sail for Fujian. When the ship sailed to Caoshidao, it hit a reef due to fog, causing the goods worth more than 300,000 taels to be completely submerged. Before the Xin Ji sailed, the guild insured the goods with Baler, Allied, Sino-American, American, American-Asia, American-China, Hanli Baoxing, and Baotai companies for a total of more than 300,000 taels and obtained insurance policies as proof. After the Xin Ji accident, the Fuzhou Guild requested compensation, but the insurance companies refused to pay on various pretexts. The guild first sued a portion of the Berlin Hamburg Land and Sea Transport Company, which had been transferred by Baoxing Company, to the Shanghai Temporary Court last September. On March 20 of this year, the court ruled that the defendant should pay the full amount and 6% annual interest. The company was cunning and refused to accept the judgment and appealed, which is still being litigated. The Baler, Allied, Sino-American, American-Asia, American, American-China, Hanli, and Baotai companies still disregard Chinese merchants and credibility and refuse to pay compensation. In addition to having resolved to deal with the situation by: (1) submitting a request to the government to order foreign insurance companies to register; (2) issuing a notice to merchants to refuse to insure with unregistered foreign insurance companies; (3) stating that the government will not accept any compensation claims from merchants who insure with unregistered companies in violation of the notice. The Shanghai Federation of Citizens specially issues a declaration to all merchants in the country to pay attention and absolutely no longer insure with the above-mentioned foreign insurance companies that refuse to pay compensation, and urge them to become aware and register with our government to exercise the scope of business and prevent future events that damage commercial credit and refuse to pay insurance claims. Furthermore, the purpose of foreign merchants establishing insurance companies is to make profits, which is also a part of economic aggression. Although the establishment of foreign insurance companies was not considered economic aggression, their operation of the insurance business in our country is not supervised by our government, so there are acts of refusing to pay compensation. This is obvious and clear economic aggression. Our country's merchants have long been anesthetized by the sweet talk and enticements of foreign insurance companies and buried under brutal economic aggression, which is countless for centuries. Now our country's merchants should also know the purpose and means of foreigners. If you don't realize it now, the future troubles will be even deeper. The Shanghai Federation of Citizens, in order to prevent and save the situation, and contribute its loyal advice, requests that our merchants be self-respecting and no longer be deceived by foreign merchants. Please be careful and hereby declare it. The Shanghai Federation of Citizens Preparatory Committee.

Central Bank Inspection Report

The Central Bank's 62nd Inspection Report on Issuance Reserves stated: In accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this committee is responsible for inspecting the preparation funds for the bank's issuance of convertible notes. The 62nd inspection was held at the bank's Issuance Bureau on August 9, 1930, and the inspection results are hereby announced as follows: The total amount of convertible notes issued was 16,820,115 silver dollars, including 15,807,388 silver dollar notes and 121,270.07 silver dollar auxiliary currency notes. The total amount of convertible note preparation funds was 16,820,115 silver dollars, including 14,225,816.60 silver dollars in cash reserves. The cash reserves consisted of 11,294,529.73 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance vault, 1,148,685.14 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,782,601.73 silver dollars stored in correspondent banks. The collateral reserve was equivalent to 2,594,298.40 silver dollars. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve was 60% and the collateral reserve was 40%. The inspection results showed that the cash reserve exceeded 60% and the collateral reserve was less than 40%, which was in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby issued. August 9, 1930. Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilu.

Anti-Opium Society Establishes Overseas Branch

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society has been extremely concerned about the suffering of overseas Chinese from the opium monopoly. Last spring, it sent the society's director-general, Huang Jiaohui, to Nanyang and other regions to promote its work, which was very effective. The leaders of the Chinese communities in Singapore in particular expressed their sympathy and began to organize anti-opium groups. For the sake of convenience, they promoted the revival of the original Zhenwu Charity Society. After four months of preparation, they elected responsible officers last month, who were sworn into office. They are now establishing branches in various British-controlled ports. The society's chairman, Chen Shunan, vice-chairman, Lin Jindian, executive committee members, Zhou Xianrui, Luo Chengde, etc., sent a letter yesterday reporting as follows: "Respected Sirs: Since opium was imported into our country more than 80 years ago, the scourge of opium has spread throughout the country. The pain and suffering have caused people throughout the country to wring their hands in anguish and fear the decline and fall of our country. We have been calling out loudly and trying to save it. Five years before the founding of the Republic of China, the Japanese first founded this society in Singapore. At the same time, the British-controlled islands of Malaya were also established. The British-controlled states of Malaya held their first anti-opium conference in Perak the following year, and the momentum was very enthusiastic. The promotion of smoking cessation was very effective. When the European War broke out in 1914, the local government banned various societies from holding meetings and discussions, and this society became inactive. However, we have never forgotten the importance of reorganizing the society and restoring its former glory. This spring, your society's director-general, Mr. Huang Jiaohui, came to Nanyang to investigate the opium situation. When he passed through Singapore, he told us about the tragic situation of the opium scourge in recent years. We were even more alarmed and rushed to call for action. On March 8, we convened a general meeting of new and old members of this society at the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce to welcome Director-General Huang and discuss the situation. We unanimously agreed to revive the society and elected a preparatory committee to carry out the process. After four months of preparation, the procedures were completed. On the 15th of last month, we held a general meeting of members to pass the constitution and hold elections. On the 20th of this month, all officers were sworn into office and held their first meeting, resolving to send letters to Chinese community leaders in various British-controlled ports to urge them to unite against opium, and to persuade our overseas Chinese to resolve to quit smoking, and to contact anti-opium groups at home and abroad to cooperate and work together to achieve the goal of eliminating opium. Your society leads the anti-opium movement and is admired throughout the country. Mr. Huang Jiaohui's mission to Nanyang has also given our society a great boost in its revival. We hereby record the case and ask for your review and guidance. We look forward to your guidance and assistance."

Printing Business Not Mortgaged to Japanese Merchants

Market Chamber of Commerce's Investigation Report

The National Society states that the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a reply to the Social Bureau, stating (the preceding part omitted): "On July 24th, we received Order No. 2601 from your bureau, relaying an order from the Municipal Government based on a request from the Sixth District Party Department to investigate whether Japanese merchants are taking advantage of the soaring gold prices to buy out Chinese-owned factories. We have forwarded the original and duplicate orders to the color and lead printing trade associations to investigate and report back. Now, on July 31st, we received a letter from the Lead Printing Trade Association stating that none of its members have sold or mortgaged their businesses to Japanese merchants, and they have earnestly advised them not to be tempted by Japanese merchants to engage in private sales or mortgages in the future. On August 6th, we received a letter from the Color Printing Trade Association stating that they have more than forty members in the same industry and have sent personnel to investigate, and have not heard of any such incidents. If the Sixth District Party Department has any knowledge, it can provide the names of the businesses for investigation and assistance." We hereby submit a document for your review and forwarding for public convenience.

Commodity Inspection Bureau Acting as Agent to Inspect Military Clothing Materials

Entrusted by the Quartermaster Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau has previously been entrusted by the Quartermaster Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs to inspect various items such as cotton and military blankets, and the inspection reports have been highly accurate. The department is very satisfied with this service. Now, the department is purchasing a large quantity of military-use khaki woolen fabric in Shanghai to be used for military uniforms. In order to determine whether the quality of the fabric meets the standards of the sample fabric, the department has specially ordered Director Yan of the Material Section of the Storage Department to travel to Shanghai to deliver a letter to the bureau requesting assistance with the inspection. The letter states that the department has ordered a large quantity of military-use khaki woolen fabric from Shanghai merchants. Detailed agreements have been made regarding the ratio of wool to cotton, the quality of cotton and wool, the number of warp and weft yarns, the weight per yard, the warp and weft density per square inch, the width, tensile strength, and insulation properties. Now, the merchant has delivered the first batch of woolen fabric, and in order to determine whether its quality meets the requirements stipulated in the signed contract, we have extracted the quality clauses from the contract and request your bureau to conduct an inspection and provide us with the results. Upon receiving the letter, the bureau immediately sent personnel to the Dahua Woolen Mill to take samples for inspection in accordance with the law.

Passenger on Small Boat Drowns in River at Night

Driver Unable to Rescue

The Xiaoguang class head small boat of the Asia Petroleum Company departed from the Xinkuan Wharf on Hankou Road at 8 PM last night, carrying passengers to the company's wharf in Pudong. While passing the Lujiazui pier, a middle-aged man suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide when no one was paying attention. The captain immediately stopped the boat to rescue him, but due to the darkness of the night, he had already disappeared without a trace. Afterwards, the second captain, Ye Xigen, reported the incident to the water police station for record. It is said that the man was wearing a white undershirt and blue cloth pants, and was about thirty years old. It is unknown what his hidden troubles were that led him to make such a resolute decision to commit suicide.

Carpenter Falls to Death

Lu Xiaorong, a carpenter aged thirty-two working at the Yangshupu Xinchengji Construction Factory, accidentally fell from a wooden scaffold while working in the factory a few days ago and died instantly. After the incident was reported, the Yangshupu Police Station ordered investigator Ye Chuanxi to investigate and verify the facts. The body was taken to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, the special district court appointed a prosecutor to examine the body and ordered it to be handed over to the deceased's brother, Lu Shurong, for burial. The factory staff also donated 170 yuan to the deceased's family.

Small Fire at Huashang Electric Company

At 3:35 PM yesterday afternoon, a fire broke out at the Huashang Electric Company in the south of Shanghai. Two large thatched houses, each divided into four small rooms, totaling eight rooms, used to store materials such as steel rails and asphalt, were unoccupied. The northern four small rooms, containing steel rails, asphalt, cement, lime, carpentry wood, and metalworking materials, suddenly caught fire for unknown reasons. Upon hearing the alarm, the company's Traffic Director Zhu Shaoyi and Engineering Section Director Song Ziyuan immediately led the employees to try their best to rescue the situation. They immediately reported to the Dongjiadu and Nanxi fire stations, which dispatched fire trucks to the scene. The fire trucks arrived quickly and bravely fought the fire. The Songhu Garrison Command also received the report and immediately dispatched a platoon of soldiers from the 26th Regiment stationed near the Gaochangmiao Arsenal, as well as the arsenal's guard team and the Gaochangmiao Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, to maintain order at the scene. The fire was extinguished at 4:10 PM. As a result, four thatched houses were destroyed, causing damage to teak, asphalt, lime, etc., totaling approximately 2,000 yuan. It is said that the fire was likely caused by the spontaneous combustion of lime and asphalt due to the hot and dry weather. Since it occurred during the day, there were no major dangers. It is said that the thatched houses were originally planned to be demolished and rebuilt as iron houses.

The Shanghai Huashang Electric Company installs meters for its subscribers and inspects them at least once every three years. Recently, it has been sending workers to remove old meters that have been installed for a long time and return them to the company for inspection, while replacing them with newly calibrated meters. This work is expected to be completed soon.

Regulations for Inspecting Pharmacists, Medicines, and Registers

Established by the Health Bureau

The Municipal Health Bureau recently drafted eight regulations for inspecting pharmacists, medicines, and registers in the city. These regulations have been submitted to the Municipal Government and approved by the Ministry of Health for record. The following is an excerpt of the regulations: Article 1: These regulations are formulated in accordance with Article 19 of the Regulations for the Management of Pharmacists. Article 2: All Chinese and Western pharmacists in the city, in addition to complying with the Regulations for the Management of Pharmacists and the Regulations for the Management of Prepared Medicines, shall also comply with the provisions of these regulations and be subject to inspection by the Health Bureau at any time. Article 3: Chinese and Western pharmacists selling medicines shall classify raw materials, prepared medicines, and narcotics, and record them in detail in the purchase and sales registers, noting the quantity of each type. In the case of prepared medicines, the permit number and date of issuance of the Ministry of Health's license shall also be indicated. Article 4: Chinese and Western pharmacists manufacturing poisonous and highly potent drugs shall, in addition to complying with Article 9 of the Regulations for the Management of Pharmacists, also record the quantity manufactured at any time in separate registers. Article 5: Whenever the Health Bureau sends personnel for inspection, Chinese and Western pharmacists shall, upon presentation of the inspector's identification, provide access to various medicine registration books and registers, and lead the inspection of various medicines. If the inspection is accurate, the inspector shall stamp the various registers to certify. Article 6: Any Chinese or Western pharmacist who violates the regulations or refuses inspection may be punished according to the circumstances, in accordance with the Regulations for the Management of Pharmacists and the Regulations for the Management of Prepared Medicines. Article 7: If there are any matters not covered by these regulations, they may be submitted for amendment at any time. Article 8: These regulations shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Municipal Government.

Tongzhou Channel Shifts Eastward and Southward

Notice from the Customs Maritime Affairs Section Patrol Engineering Department: This Patrol Engineering Department has investigated the eastward shift of the Tongzhou Channel within the boundaries of the Jianghai Customs Tax Office. The circumstances are listed below: The Tongzhou Channel in the Yangtze River has shifted eastward and southward from its original location by 15% of an English mile. The remaining circumstances remain the same. The new mooring point is south 40 degrees and three-quarters east of the Xuliujingzui stake, a distance of 5 English miles. According to the compass direction, the nautical chart No. 3 published by the Maritime Affairs Bureau should be corrected accordingly. This is to be followed and notified to all ships, which should pay attention and remember carefully to avoid negligence. Issued on August 8th, 19th year of the Republic of China.

It was resolved to appoint Cheng Qiusheng. In addition, association members must uniformly find a guarantor. 9. Yu Tianbao inquired about the registration of industry and commerce. It was resolved to calculate from the date of entry into the shop and issue a letter for reference. 11. The association's tea boy, Lu Shengdu, requested a subsidy. It was resolved that there was no such precedent. 12. The association should immediately resume dinner parties to promote friendship among colleagues. It was resolved to recommend Committee Member Chen Tiansheng to draft the organizational regulations. 13. The detailed rules for the operation of the association's various departments should be drafted quickly. Local News

Ransom Victim Safely Escapes After Being Kidnapped

Chen Dezhong, owner of Yingfeng Silk Factory

Suddenly Kidnapped by Bandits Yesterday Morning

A Herd of Water Buffalo Blocks the Way

Bandits Abandon Victim and Flee Upon Seeing Pursuers

Chen Dezhong, the owner of Yingfeng Silk Factory in Tanhuaqiao, Pushan Road, Zhabei, and a native of Huzhou, lives at No. 4 Zhili Bi Yanghang, Xinkang Road, Second Malu, in the public concession. He goes to the factory every morning to manage the factory affairs in his own car, concession permit No. 8850, municipal government permit No. 6263. He employs a driver, Xu Yuncheng, from Taizhou. Yesterday morning at 8:30 AM, he had breakfast at home and went to the factory as usual, not expecting that disaster was about to befall him.

Sudden Armed Kidnapping

Chen Dezhong arrived at the factory around 8:50 AM. Since the factory's products have not been of good quality recently, he planned to visit Baotai Silk Factory in Rihuiqiao, South City. He summoned six employees and ordered the driver, Xu Yuncheng, to drive there. However, when the car passed Pushan Villa, four kidnappers suddenly appeared. Two were wearing blue short shirts and pants, one was wearing a white short shirt and pants, and one was wearing gray short shirts and pants. Three of them pulled out guns and warned everyone not to make a sound.

Chen Dezhong is Kidnapped

Although there were many people in the car at the time, they were all intimidated by the weapons and remained silent. The six employees were driven out of the car by the bandits, and one bandit grabbed Chen, turned the car east, and drove towards Dachang. The evicted employees watched as their factory owner was kidnapped, but were unable to call for help and had to report to the Tanhuaqiao security group for assistance.

Water Buffalo Blocks the Way

After obtaining the ransom victim, the kidnappers sped eastward at full speed. Unexpectedly, when passing near the Taiyangmiao Road Pingjiang Public Office, a herd of water buffalo suddenly appeared ahead, moving slowly. The bandit driving the car honked the horn frantically, but the stupid water buffalo ran around in all directions upon hearing the sound. Two of them suddenly ran into the road. The bandits, fearing an accident, panicked and crashed the car into the wall of the public office.

Gripping Ransom Victim's Hands

At the same time, the ransom victim seized the opportunity to stop the car engine. The engine was damaged instantly and could not be started. The bandits were terrified. One bandit gripped the ransom victim's hands tightly and pressed his head down to hide him in the car. Another bandit got out of the car to inspect the damage, intending to drive again.

Kidnappers Flee

After Chen was kidnapped, the evicted employees immediately reported to the security group. Soon, the Taiyangmiao police station of the fourth district, as well as the fourth district headquarters and the detective team, received the report and rushed to the scene with police officers. The bandits saw the detectives coming from afar and knew that their plan had failed. They abandoned the ransom victim and fled in all directions.

Ransom Victim Survives Narrow Escape

Chen Dezhong, seeing that the bandits had fled, jumped out of the car and hired a rickshaw to return to the factory. On the way, he met Zhang Shaotang, a silk factory donor, and told him about his narrow escape. He also went to report to the fourth district headquarters police station, and the detectives pursued the bandits for several hours, but failed to capture any of them.

Uncle's Kidnapping of Nephew Case Judgment

Russian and Song Sentenced to Five Years Imprisonment and Deportation

To Be Sent to Inland Authorities for Further Punishment

Last month, a sensational case of an uncle kidnapping his nephew occurred at the residence of Mrs. Chen Xing, an elderly woman residing at No. 2 Huabao Alley, Lagenna Road, French Concession. The case has been thoroughly investigated by the special investigation unit of the French Police, including Detective Inspector Jin Jiulin, Chief Detective Li Yaolong, Deputy Detectives Mao Jingen, Qian Yumin, Wang Rusong, and patrol detectives Zhou Yaoting, Zhang Ziying, Zhou Buguang, and others. The main culprits, Luo Henglin, Song Wusheng (also known as Song Huaiqing), as well as Yuan Tianming, Bao Zhiming, and suspects Zhou A'er, Zhou Weixiang, and others, seven in total, were apprehended, and the kidnap victim was rescued. As previously reported, yesterday, the police handed over the group to the French Court for prosecution. Western Inspector Sazier first explained the background, stating that after the plaintiff's grandson was kidnapped, the perpetrators demanded a ransom of over 100,000 yuan, arranging a meeting in Ningbo Road, leading to the case's breakthrough. Subsequently, Attorney Ba He, representing the plaintiff, stated that the plaintiff was too old to appear in court. The first defendant, Luo Henglin, the uncle of the plaintiff's grandson Chen Yongkang, daringly colluded with outsiders to kidnap and demand ransom, was extremely unlawful and requested severe punishment according to the law. Furthermore, the plaintiff's side greatly admired the police's swift detection and resolution of the case and wished to allocate 500 yuan as a reward to the detectives. When questioned, Luo Henglin confessed that he was from Jiaxing and used to be in the foreign goods business, but recently lost his job and, out of desperation, colluded with Song Wusheng and the fugitive Chen A'gen to kidnap his nephew in hopes of extorting money. Song Wusheng confessed that he was previously a secret agent for the Songhu Garrison Headquarters. Luo Henglin had asked Zhu Shanhe to discuss with him the kidnapping of the plaintiff's grandson, so he introduced Chen A'gen to arrange the kidnapping. At the time, Luo said he could get at least 160,000 to 170,000 yuan, and promised to give him 20% of the reward after it was done, but although he knew about it, he didn't assist with the kidnapping. The rest gave evasive answers and hired lawyers to defend themselves. Yuan Tianming confessed that he was sent by Chen A'gen to negotiate with the plaintiff for the money. Bao Zhiming confessed that Chen A'gen sent him to monitor Yuan Tianming's negotiations with the plaintiff. Zhou A'er, Zhou Weixiang, and others all stated that they came to Shanghai and were mistakenly arrested by the detectives, knowing nothing about the kidnapping and requesting a clear investigation. Judge Zhu, the French Consul presiding over the case, sentenced Luo Henglin and Song Wusheng each to five years in the Western Prison, followed by deportation and transfer to inland authorities for punishment. Yuan Tianming and Bao Zhiming were each sentenced to four years in the Western Prison, after which they would be permanently expelled from the Concession. Zhou A'er and Zhou Weixiang were released without charge. The 500 yuan offered by the plaintiff was transferred to the General Inspector to be distributed as rewards to the detectives who handled the case.

Numerous Knife Wounds on Female Corpse

Face Hacked Beyond Recognition

Neck Bones and Fingers Severed

Seemingly Killed by Multiple Assailants

The Horrific Sight Was Unbearable to Witness

Yesterday morning, a female corpse was discovered in a pond dug by villagers at the end of Gonghe Xin Road in Zhabei. The body was covered in blood and flesh, unrecognizable. The Fifth District Police Station investigated and ordered Tan Maokun, the local warden of Que San Tu, to report to the Land Court. Xu, the prosecutor, and Shen, the coroner, were appointed to the scene for examination. The female corpse was found to be about twenty years old, wearing a Xiangyun gauze shirt and pants, with her hair already cut off. Her body had numerous knife wounds, and her face was hacked beyond recognition. The neck bones were severed, and many fingers were cut off. The sight was too horrific to witness. It was suspected that she had been killed by multiple assailants after resisting, resulting in the loss of her fingers. The cause of death was determined to be from injuries, and the body was disposed of at that location after death. Photographs were taken, and the body was collected by the charity and placed in a temporary coffin while the investigation into the killer(s) continues.

Fat Cow Bursts With Wild Nature

Rams Through the Streets into Nanhai Goods Store

Smashes Jars and Leaves a Pile of Feces

Shen Linsheng, the owner of Tiancheng Nanhai Goods Store in Caojiadu Town, Shanghai West, has been privately raising several dairy cows without a license to sell milk. Because this area is a prosperous market, he lets his cattle roam in the open spaces near commercial shops and residential houses every day, causing them to trample plants, smash bamboo fences, and cause other damage. The businessmen and residents have suffered greatly. However, due to the friendly relations of neighbors, there was no need to intervene, but yesterday at about 7 PM several cows grazed on the vacant area behind Laogong Mao Store. One of the fat dairy cows suddenly got excited and rushed recklessly to the point where it smashed a bamboo fence of a certain family. It leaped from the small lane and raced into town (that is, the extremely busy Great Western Road) and went straight to Lisanjiaochang, and straight to Dashunfeng Nanhai Goods Store, rushing into the shop, the kitchen, and the earthen jars and other objects, all being smashed. The shop's staff feared something dreadful would happen, so they called the police. They all came to drive the cow away. The cow also left a pile of dung in the hall before leaving. People fled and panicked. When Mr. Shen learned of this he went there and stopped the cow. The police on duty took the owner of the cow, Shen Linsheng, back to the Sixth District Police Station for questioning.

Municipal Government Emphasizes Public Hygiene

Fruit Vendors Must Use Gauze Covers

Municipal Health Bureau Ordered to Conduct Regular Inspections

Recently, various fruit stalls along the roadsides in the South City have been selling various kinds of fruits, attracting swarms of flies. Although the Municipal Health Bureau has strictly ordered compliance with regulations to use gauze covers, there are still many vendors who have not complied. The Municipal Government believes that as the weather is hot, eating carelessly can easily lead to illness, making it necessary to take practical measures to prohibit this practice. Yesterday, it specially instructed the Health Bureau to immediately work with the Public Security Bureau to send personnel to conduct inspections and eliminate these practices in order to emphasize hygiene.

Municipal Government Prohibits Obscene Materials

Approval of Interior Ministry's Dispatch

To the Public Security Bureau, Order

The Municipal Government yesterday instructed the Public Security Bureau: "Regarding the matter of complying with orders, we have received Dispatch No. 631 from the Interior Ministry, which states: 'Regarding the matter of dispatching, we have received Dispatch No. 13797 from the Ministry of Finance, which states: "Regarding the matter of dispatching, we have received a report from the General Affairs Department, which reports that the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, Mei Weiliang, reported that on April 4th of this year, the Parcel Office of his Customs intercepted a registered package No. 81194 containing three-dimensional glass mirrors embedded with obscene pictures. The cover indicated that it was sent from Hamburg, Germany (Heyh, Brochelmannxca, Barkhor, Hamburg) to Lu Lin Foreign Firm, 62 Jiangxi Road, Shanghai. In addition to detaining the obscene pictures and sending three copies for inspection, the remaining mirrored pictures have been destroyed according to regulations. We hereby report for your review and approval." Three samples of the obscene picture mirrors are attached. Based on this, regarding the prohibition of transporting obscene materials, according to the methods stipulated in your ministry's Order No. 1944, if obscene materials imported from other countries are seized, three copies should be sent to the Interior Ministry for review and processing, while the remainder should be detained and destroyed. This has been complied with in the past. Now, based on the previous report, we have enclosed the original obscene picture mirrors for your review and submission to the Interior Ministry for review and processing.' Three copies of the obscene picture mirrors are attached. While this matter was being processed, we successively received Dispatches No. 1382 from the ministry, stating: 'Regarding the matter of sending, the Customs Commissioner of the Customs Department reported that regarding the prohibition of transporting obscene materials, according to the methods stipulated in your ministry's Order No. 1944, if obscene materials imported from other countries are seized, three copies should be sent to the Interior Ministry for review and processing, while the remainder should be detained and destroyed to prevent their spread. This has been complied with in the past. Now, we have successively received reports from the Customs Commissioners of the Jiaohai Customs, Huo Lijia; the Jianghai Customs, Mei Weiliang; the Yanji Customs Office, Huo Lijia, Letu; and the Changsha Customs Office, Mou'ergen, who have all submitted samples of the obscene materials seized from abroad in accordance with the general order for review and forwarding. We hereby enclose the original reports from the various Customs Commissioners, six in total, along with a copy of a paper and six sets of obscene materials for your review and forwarding to the Interior Ministry for review and processing.' Six original reports, a copy of a paper, and a package of obscene materials are attached. Based on this, we are copying the original reports and attaching a package of obscene materials to this dispatch for your review and processing. Dispatch No. 13813 states: 'Regarding the matter of dispatching, the Customs Commissioner of the Customs Department reported that regarding the prohibition of transporting obscene materials, according to the methods stipulated in your ministry's Order No. 1944, if obscene materials imported from other countries are seized, three copies should be sent to the Interior Ministry for review and processing, while the remainder should be detained and destroyed to prevent their spread. This has been complied with in the past. Now, the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, Mei Weiliang, reported that on June 5th, the Parcel Office of his Customs intercepted a registered package No. 91522 containing sixty-one foreign picture cards, forty-two of which were obscene pictures. The cover indicated that it was sent from Paris, Librairie Pigalle, 45 Rue Lipic, Paris (I8me), to Monsieur Victor Candurt, Cathay Hotel, Shanghai. In addition to sending three samples for your review and forwarding, the remaining cards have been destroyed according to regulations. We hereby report for your review and forwarding to the Interior Ministry for review and processing.' Three obscene pictures are attached. Based on this, we have enclosed the original document for your review and processing.' Three obscene pictures are attached. With the approval of this investigation, the obscene materials have been strictly prohibited by the 1923 International Convention on the Prohibition of Obscene Publications, and this Ministry has repeatedly issued orders for their prohibition. In addition to responding to the various previous reports and circulating them for prohibition, we hereby request that you investigate and order compliance with this matter. This order is hereby issued."

Boat Owners and Others Request Dredging of Nanhuiguan and Other Wharves Again

Boat owner representatives Xing Zhigang and others yesterday submitted a petition to the Municipal Port Authority again, requesting the dredging of Nanhuiguan and other ports, stating that they were petitioning for the dredging of ports to facilitate transportation. They stated that they had previously submitted a petition to the Municipal Government requesting the allocation of large funds to order your bureau to dredge the riverside beaches and reorganize water transportation to maintain navigation, etc. The reply was that although a comprehensive dredging would be costly and have far-reaching effects, it would not be easy to implement at the moment and could be delayed for now. Upon investigation, the Nanhuiguan Wharf and Wanyu Wharf have long been the places where east-west boats from the Pudong area dock in Shanghai. During the seventh year of Xianfeng of the Qing Dynasty, December (1857), merchants such as Deji, Daheng, Wanxiang, Senmao, Hecheng, and Wanyu petitioned Huang, the Shanghai County Magistrate, to erect stone tablets at each of the ports, granting permanent docking rights. To this day, the stone tablets still exist and the writing is clear. A simple inspection will reveal that although the wharves are often repaired, the sand and mud on both sides have accumulated more and more. There are also sampans squatting on the wharves, treating them as homes, so that boats coming to Shanghai cannot dock and have to stay far out in the river. Passengers and goods cannot get on and off safely. It is believed that Shanghai is a world-renowned commercial port, relying entirely on the convenience of port transportation. The Nanhuiguan Wharf is also a famous port in the South City, the lifeline of commerce. Each day, it is relied upon by no less than thousands of people, and the goods transferred are worth no less than tens of thousands of taels of silver. The amount of ship tax paid is also not small. Your bureau is in charge of port transportation and should plan in detail to facilitate transportation. Therefore, we jointly petition your honor to approve the removal of obstacles such as sampans at the Nanhuiguan, Wanyu, Gongyi, and other wharves, and prohibit them from docking. Survey the earthworks and engage in dredging to maintain navigation and facilitate transportation.

Xue Cheng Innocent

Bizarre Marriage Lawsuit

Wang Jinbao Willing to Be Second Wife

Gao Bingjiang Admits Visiting Prostitutes

Wang Lu, a woman from Ningbo, and her daughter Genbao recently filed a lawsuit in the French Court against Gao Bingjiang, who resides on the upper floor of Xingxin Soy Sauce Garden at No. 1022 Huade Road in the Public Concession, accusing him of seducing a virgin, breaking his promise, and publicly insulting them, requesting the court to investigate and prosecute him. Her complaint states that she only has one daughter named Genbao, who is 18 years old. In the winter of the sixteenth year (1927), she rented the upper floor of the soy sauce garden opened by Gao Bingjiang. Unexpectedly, in March of the following year, the defendant took advantage of her absence and seduced Genbao. At that time, Genbao was only 16 years old. When she found out that her daughter had been seduced, she immediately scolded her daughter and questioned the defendant that since he already had a wife, he should not seduce a virgin. The defendant then asked Chen Zhiqin, a fellow villager, to mediate. Bingjiang was willing to marry Genbao as a second wife. Seeing that the matter was a foregone conclusion, she reluctantly agreed for the sake of her reputation. On the first day of the tenth month of that year, he sent a gold ring and a marriage proposal card in the name of his brother Gao Shunsheng. Following Ningbo customs, she also gave a reply card, agreeing to set another date for the betrothal gifts. However, since then, the defendant transferred his shop to someone else and avoided meeting them, and the marriage was delayed. She was very surprised and asked the original matchmaker, Chen Zhiqin, to search for the defendant everywhere, but he could not be found. It was not until March of this year that she learned that the defendant was now living on Huade Road. She went to find him with her daughter, but the defendant changed his attitude and cursed them when the marriage was mentioned. She had no choice but to drag the defendant to the police station. The defendant still admitted the marriage agreement, but when the case was brought to court, the defendant denied the marriage, falsely claiming that her daughter was a prostitute and admitting to visiting prostitutes. They were fined in transit and quarreled everywhere. Afterwards, she still asked the original matchmaker to inquire about the date the defendant would fulfill the marriage, but he completely denied it. Therefore, she submitted evidence and requested the court to summon him to be punished accordingly. The summons for the hearing was issued yesterday, but the defendant did not appear for excuses. The court ordered him to be detained and the case to be reviewed.

False Report of a Child's Death to Deceive for a Coffin

The Insidiousness of Human Hearts Is Evident Here

The coffin distribution society attached to the Yongyi Benevolent Hall in Caojiadu, Shanghai West, is funded by philanthropists and merchants. The regulations stipulate that to give a coffin, it must be introduced by a merchant and verified by the society before the coffin is distributed to ensure that the matter is true. The afternoon before yesterday, a certain merchant introduced a case, reporting that the family of a Cheng, a Jiangbei native living in Hambei, had a 12-year-old boy who suddenly fell ill and died, and they were too poor to afford a coffin. They requested the society to approve the distribution of a coffin. After receiving the report, the society immediately sent investigator Zhu Guisan to the address for investigation in accordance with the regulations. However, as soon as Zhu arrived in front of the Cheng's house, several people stopped Zhu and said that the boy had been dead for two days and that the weather was too hot, causing him to decay, and asked him not to enter to avoid infection. Zhu thought that the rules of the society stipulated that he must investigate the truth, so he boldly entered and saw someone silently lying in the bed. He stared at it for about three minutes and suddenly saw movement in the bed. He suspected something was wrong and stepped forward to lift the quilt. He saw a child staring with his eyes, sweating profusely on his forehead. He carefully observed that the child seemed to be ill but was definitely not dead. Zhu immediately returned to the society and reported that the Cheng family had falsely reported the death to deceive for a coffin. Fortunately, the coffin had not yet been carried to the house. The insidiousness of human hearts today is evident here.

Passenger Dies After Jumping Out of Train Window

The day before yesterday, on the Shanghai-Ningbo line, a passenger, about twenty years old and wearing a blue cloth shirt and pants, jumped out of the train window as it approached the North Station platform. It is suspected that he did not purchase a ticket. He fell onto the tracks and suffered serious injuries, unable to speak. He was immediately sent to Renji Hospital by the police but died before he could be treated. Yesterday, Yan Liugen, the warden of Ji Yi Tu, reported the case to the Land Court. Prosecutor Xu and others arrived at the scene for examination and ordered the body to be collected for burial.

Bandit in Little Lion Kidnapping Case Changes Testimony

Claims He Was Just Taking the Child to Play

Court Orders Summons of Rice Cake Vendor

Chen Huanwen, Jiang Wenxuan, Yang Zhaoxian, and Yang Wang, along with others, kidnapped Xiao Shizi, the four-year-old son of Wu Guisheng, who runs a restaurant at the Youche Wharf, on July 23rd. The next day, the First Section of the First District apprehended the bandits and rescued the hostage in Zhoujiaqiao, Shanghai West. After interrogation, the defendants confessed and were transferred to the Land Court for investigation and prosecution. However, the defendants changed their testimony, claiming it was not a kidnapping because Chen Huanwen and the victim's son were cousins and he was just taking him to play. Therefore, Judge Niu opened the court again yesterday for further investigation. According to the victim Wu Guisheng, 45 years old, from Yancheng, who runs a restaurant at the Youche Wharf in Nanshi, Xiao Shizi is my son. On the day of the kidnapping, I went to Nanhai Putuoshan to offer incense and returned home to find that he had already been rescued. It was on July 23rd. My wife went out to buy groceries and left Xiao Shizi at home. At that time, Chen Huanwen also came to my house. Chen Huanwen is related to me by marriage. Later, my son disappeared. According to the rice cake vendor, my son was taken away. My wife suspected Chen Huanwen, so she asked my brother-in-law Zhao Ronghua to look for him. Zhao found Chen Huanwen's mother-in-law, Yang Zhaoxian's mother, and met Yang Zhaoxian, who confessed, so he reported it to the police and they were arrested. But after being kidnapped, they did not ask us for money. Wu Zhang, 45 years old, testified that after entrusting Zhao Ronghua to search, she received a letter the next day instructing her to go to Yinghua Street, saying that Yang Zhaoxian's accomplices were there. She dragged them to the police station, but they were not accepted. The police station then sent a patrol officer with police to Zhoujiaqiao to solve the case. Zhao Ronghua, 41 years old, from Shou County, Anhui, testified that Xiao Shizi disappeared on the 23rd of last month. Wu Zhang ordered her brother to come to me and asked me to look for the Chen family. I went to Yang Zhaoxian's mother's house and asked, and she said that he had gone with Yang Zhaoxian, but she did not know about the child. The next day, I went to Yang's mother-in-law Wang's house to investigate. Later, Yang Zhaoxian came, and Wang asked my second son-in-law, Xu, to call me. I said to Yang Zhaoxian, "If you hand over the person, I will give you 20 or 30 yuan." He refused at first, and I wanted to call the detectives, so he gave me the address, which was in the straw shed at No. 12 Zhoujiaqiao. At that time, three men and one woman, and Xiao Shizi, five people in total, were arrested. There were three reed mats inside. Patrol Officer Zhang Haizhu, 33 years old, from Beiping, currently residing in the First Section of the First District, testified that at 3 or 4 AM on the night of July 24th, we received a report and took a car with Yang Zhaoxian to the straw shed in Zhoujiaqiao and ordered Yang Zhaoxian to knock on the door. We entered and arrested them. The testimony of patrolman Liu Chunxi, 35 years old, from Tai'an, Shandong, first-class patrolman, was roughly the same. The judge then questioned the defendants, who all gave evasive answers and did not admit to being kidnappers. Because the circumstances of the case were strange, the judge ordered that the debate not be opened and that the rice cake vendor and Wu Zhang's brother be summoned for further investigation. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Zhang Chunguang Hangs Himself After Mourning a Friend

Cause Unknown

Zhang Chunguang, 41 years old, a native of Chaozhou, has been the manager of Jin Yu Pawnshop at No. 97 Quanzhang Hall, Limalu, Sixteenth Shop, Nanshi, for more than 20 years. A few days ago, Zhang's sworn friend, Chen, who opened Yongtai Pawnshop in the Baxianqiao area of ​​the North City, suddenly passed away. Zhang, after hearing the news, went to mourn him the day before yesterday. Around 7 o'clock in the evening, he returned to the store. After dinner, around 12:00 AM, the pawnshop was closed. Because his family lived in the back of the house, Zhang returned to his bedroom. Then, around 1:00 AM yesterday morning, Zhang groped in the dark to the shop, reached out, and opened the drawer of the counter. He was heard by the shopkeeper, who was awakened from his sleep. The shopkeeper asked what was happening, Zhang then closed the drawer, saying it was nothing, and went back to the room. The shopkeeper went back to sleep. Then, Zhang's wife, Zhu, suddenly remembered that her husband had been out for a long time and had not returned, she became suspicious, got up, and called the shopkeeper to search everywhere, but could not find him. When they were led to the package room upstairs, they suddenly saw Zhang had hung himself from the beam with a belt. They felt his body and found that he was already dead. They reported the matter to the chief of the First District, who ordered Lu Yongde, the landlord of the Sixteenth Shop, to report to the Shanghai Land Court to appoint a prosecutor to investigate the scene.

Two Floating Corpses in Shanghai

(1) Yesterday morning around 7 o'clock, an unidentified girl's corpse was discovered floating in the Suzhou River under Fujian Road Bridge. The girl was approximately seven or eight years old, and no one has claimed her. Subsequently, a Chinese constable, No. 29, from the Water Police Station came across the body and had it retrieved and sent to the Life Saving Bureau for collection. (2) Again, at 10 o'clock in the morning, an unidentified male corpse floated to the surface of the Huangpu River near the China Merchants Bureau's Jin Li Yuan wharf. The man was wearing a blue cloth shirt and trousers, with sores on his head. He was approximately thirty years old. The Life Saving Bureau's patrol boat retrieved the body and transported it to the Bureau for collection.

Lodger Commits Suicide by Poison

Yesterday afternoon, at around 2 o'clock, a customer arrived at the Jiangsu Inn, Mantingfang, Wuma Road, wearing a twill shirt and trousers, appearing to be an intellectual. He only wrote his name as Lu Zhongde, a local resident, seventeen years old, in the guest register. After the tea server led him to room 55, he paid the room fee. Before long, he went out wearing a hat and returned at around 6 o'clock in the evening. It is unknown what caused him to secretly consume lysol. By 10 o'clock, the poison took effect, and his groans reached outside the room. At first, the tea server and others suspected he was suffering from heatstroke, but gradually his complexion turned pale, his eyes became fixed, and his mouth remained open. The accountant's office promptly notified the Old Gate Police Station, which dispatched Chinese Constable No. 2706 to arrive and transport him by vehicle to Renji Hospital for treatment. His life is said to be in critical condition.

Axes and Pistols Fired Together

Yun Xiaorong Severely Injured

Yun Xiaorong, a thirty-two-year-old Nanjing native, currently resides on Shantou Road in the Public Concession and is an unemployed hooligan. He previously worked as a protector in various gambling dens in the Public Concession (commonly known as "baotaijiao"). Later, when all the gambling dens were completely closed, he was also eliminated. When Yun was protecting gambling dens, he had two close companions named Ma Pi Fa and Fang Xiaomao, who spent their days together. However, a few weeks ago, Yun suddenly had a quarrel with Ma Pi and Fang, which then turned into a physical fight. Initially, Fang Xiaomao was beaten up once by Yun, who had gathered a group of people. Fang then held a grudge and called upon Ma Pi and others every day to search for Yun everywhere to seek revenge, but they did not encounter him for several days. Later, Fang learned that Yun was currently hiding in the home of Fan Asi at No. 6 Yuqingfang, Maide'an Road, in the French Concession, smoking opium. Yesterday morning at 11:30, he gathered six or seven people, including Ma Pi Fa, and went straight to Yuqingfang to wait. At that time, Yun was just walking out of No. 4, intending to go to No. 6 to smoke opium. As soon as he approached the entrance of No. 7, Fang and others rushed forward, each using pistols and axes to wildly chop at Yun's body, firing two shots. One bullet pierced Yun's right thigh, causing him to immediately fall to the ground, bleeding profusely. A total of six axes struck his legs, and one axe struck each of his hands, breaking his foot bones. Seeing that their goal had been achieved, the assailants fled the alley and disappeared without a trace. Someone reported it to the Great Bell Police Station, and the head constable immediately dispatched detectives to investigate. He also ordered Chinese Constable No. 323 to send Yun to Renji Hospital. According to the doctor, the injuries were very severe, and even if his life was spared, it would take more than two months to recover.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the coastal areas and Ma'an Island around here would be mostly cloudy with showers and strong gusts of wind from the north or northeast. The weather between the mouth of the Yangtze River and Kyushu-Geomun Island is extremely bad, with a major cyclone, because a strong hurricane has reached the northwest of Dajiao Island and is heading north or northwest. There is a northeast wind on the Yellow Sea. Also, within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 95.2 degrees and the lowest was 76.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 91.8 degrees and the lowest was 7.70 degrees.

Letter to the Editor

To the esteemed Editor:

I am writing to you because the "News" column of your esteemed newspaper today contains a report entitled "Delivery Note Packages Not Affixed with Stamps." Although this notice was issued by the Transportation Department, it is unknown on what basis it was issued. Upon investigation, the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Railways have not issued any regulations recently (the Transportation Department's notice is based on the regulations of March 28, which contains a major misunderstanding). Our Bureau specializes in handling stamp duties for delivery notes and has not received any explicit orders from superiors to waive the affixing of stamps, nor has there been any official document canceling our Bureau. We have already submitted a request to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau to await instructions. This matter concerns the future of tax revenue and must be urgently corrected to avoid misunderstandings. I hope you will publish this letter in the "Letters to the Editor" column to maintain our friendship.

With best wishes,

Chen Yan, Jiangsu Stamp Tax Railway Delivery Note Stamp Bureau

August 11th

The Successes and Failures of the Chinese Expedition Football Team in Batavia

Great Victory Over Batavia... Five to One

Crushing Defeat by Batavia Combined... Two to Six

| Li Huitang, Li Ning, and others Injured Again | Chen Yutian Rushed from Shanghai |

(July 27th, Batavia Dispatch) After the Chinese Expedition Football Team went to Java from Singapore, they competed twice in Bandung. On the 23rd, they played against the Bandung Selection Team, resulting in a 1-1 draw. On the 24th, they played against the Uni Team, resulting in a 0-1 loss for China. After the Chinese team returned to Batavia, they had two games at Ligapala on the 26th and 27th. The first was a contest with the Batavia team, which resulted in a 5-1 victory for China. The second day was the final against the Batavia Selection, which ended in a 2-6 defeat. The battle conditions of the two days are recorded as follows:

Great Victory Over Batavia

Five to One

At 4:45 PM on Saturday the 26th, the Chinese and Batavia teams entered the field one after the other and took their positions. After the referee blew the whistle to announce the start of the game, our Consul General performed the opening kick ceremony. The result of the game was a 5-1 victory for China.

Four to One in the First Half

The Chinese team's forwards received the ball, and five players attacked simultaneously, coordinating well and nearly reaching the Batavia goal. The center forward passed the ball to Cao on the right wing, who then passed it to the left wing, but it was cleared by the opposing inner defender. Sun, the center back, passed it again to the right wing. The flying general charged straight at the goal alone, causing panic among the opposing inner defenders, who mistakenly touched the ball, resulting in a penalty kick. The center forward, Dai, took the kick. As the whistle blew, the ball rolled into the corner of the goal. Before long, in the next play, the Batavia team tried to retaliate, and their five forwards attacked bravely. Fortunately, the Chinese team's inner defenders defended powerfully, and they were unable to succeed. At this time, they attacked and we defended, advancing and retreating. After about ten minutes of battle, the Batavia right wing seized the ball and dribbled it straight up, kicking it towards the Chinese goal. Zhou, the goalkeeper, tackled the ball, causing it to hit the ground. The ball was about to enter the goal, but it was hooked out of bounds by the inner defender. A corner kick was awarded; otherwise, this goal would have been scored. After a while, the Batavia forwards seized the ball again, passing it to each other and heading straight into the Chinese inner defense. With lightning speed, they kicked the ball into the Chinese goal. Ten minutes later, Cao, the right wing, received a ball passed from the center back and dribbled it straight up, nearly reaching the opposing goal before passing it to Dai, the center forward. Dai kicked the ball, and it went into the net. This was at 5:10. Two minutes later, Dai received another ball passed from the right wing and, taking advantage of the opponent's inner weakness, broke through the Batavia goal again. Three minutes later, Chen, the left wing, seized the enemy's ball and passed it to the right wing auxiliary, Chen Jiaqiu. Chen, the right wing auxiliary, sent it into the enemy's goal with a header. At halftime, the Chinese team had a 4-1 lead.

One to Zero in the Second Half

After the break, Liang Rongde replaced Chen Zhenhe as the left center back, and Chen, the right wing auxiliary, was changed to right wing, and Cao, the right wing, was changed to right wing auxiliary. After a while, the inner defender Li was injured and fell to the ground, and Li Huitang took his place. Liang Rongde became the left wing auxiliary, and the reserve player Fu Xiangqing became the left center back. Both sides fought until 6 o'clock without any gains or losses. At 6:03, the center forward Dai received a ball from Chen, the left wing, and attacked the opponent's goal again, scoring another goal. When the whistle blew to end the game, the Chinese team defeated Batavia by a score of 5-1. On this day, the winner received a trophy jointly presented by Lin Shuiqing and Chen Fuding, as well as trophies from the Silawaharora and Wuliayan factories. The losers received a silver medal from the Xu Li Company. The total ticket revenue for the day was over 9,000 guilders.

(Two) Crushing Defeat by Batavia Combined

Two to Six

On Sunday, the 27th, the Chinese team played the final against the Batavia Selection Team in the afternoon. The audience was larger than on the first day, with ticket revenues reaching over 10,000 guilders, as it was expected that today's match would be more spectacular. However, because many of the Chinese team's players had sore feet and the reinforcements had not yet arrived, although Mr. Chen Yutian had accepted the invitation to come south to take a position at a certain insurance company, he had not practiced for a long time and might not be able to join the team. Those in the know had long predicted that it would be difficult to win, but they never expected that they would lose so badly by a score of 2-6.

Center Back Sun Retaliates with a Goal

At 4:30, Mr. Hong Yuanyuan first presented a cigarette factory trophy that had not been prepared and presented the previous day. Then, Provincial Assembly Member Yang Hengjian performed the opening kick ceremony. The selected team took the offensive from the start. In less than five minutes, the Chinese team was scored upon. However, four minutes later, the five Chinese forwards coordinated their passes and attacked the opponent's goal. Suddenly, they were repelled. The ball was received by center back Sun. The opponent was unable to defend in time, and he retaliated with a goal.

Injured Soldiers and a Disordered Battle Line

By 4:50, the Chinese team's inner defense was weak, and the opponent took the opportunity to score another goal. Before long, inner defender Li Ning was injured and fell to the ground. At this time, the Chinese team's line-up changed greatly again. Because Li Ning was injured and left the field, Li Huitang had already been reassigned to left inner defender, Fu Xiangqing replaced Liang Rongde as center back, and Liang was changed to left wing auxiliary. At 5:10, the selected team's forward dribbled the ball straight in and, taking advantage of the fact that Li Huitang was standing in front of goalkeeper Zhou and could not block him, kicked in another goal. At halftime, the selected team had a 3-1 lead.

The Situation is Dire, and There is No Way to Recover

After the lemon quenched their thirst, they fought again. Although their desire for revenge was strong, there were few opportunities. At 5:30 and 5:45, the opponent scored two consecutive goals. At this point, Li Huitang returned to his original position. At 5:49, he kicked in a goal against the opponent. However, three minutes later, the opponent scored another goal. When the game stopped, the Chinese team lost by a score of 2-6. The Tiansheng Daily, Jingbao, and Angosmi trophies were all won by the Batavia Selection Team, while the silver medal from Xu Li Company was won by the defeated Chinese team.

Rotary Cup Tennis Tournament

Begins on the 15th of This Month

Yesterday's Meeting of National Representatives

At 12:30 yesterday (the 11th), the National Sports Advancement Association convened a meeting of Shanghai's national representatives at the Old Carlton Restaurant. Those present included Rotary Club President Fletcher Whiteyear (British), Gros (German), Uchida Hidesaburo (Japanese), Utto (Swiss), Hu Xiansheng (Chinese), Kaipos (Portuguese), Yiping (American), and the Association's main officials, He Boyang and Secretary Zhou Jiaqi. He Boyang, the chairman, discussed all matters related to this year's Rotary Cup competition. Then, Rotary Club President Fletcher gave a speech about the purpose of the cup, mainly to increase interest in maritime tennis and to connect the feelings of various countries. The decided matters are listed below:

1. The cup is named the Rotary Cup.

2. All competitions will be held on the grass courts of the China Tennis Club.

3. There are no restrictions on registration, but each team is limited to four people for each competition. Four doubles matches will be played by two people in rotation.

4. Each army will adopt an elimination system (no challenge matches).

5. The committee elected Chairman Hu Xiansheng as the chief referee.

6. Each country will recommend two referees, who will be appointed by the Advancement Association.

7. The competition is scheduled to begin on the 15th.

8. Please ask Mr. Fletcher to determine the order of competition.

The entire order of competition is determined as follows:

Japan, United States, United Kingdom, Switzerland, Germany, Portugal, China
